class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="/\xc9\x9b/: &#39;e&#39; in &#39;dress&#39;">\xc9\x9b</span><span title="&#39;v&#39; in &#39;vie&#39;">v</span><span title="/\xc9\x99n/: &#39;on&#39; in &#39;button&#39;">\xc9\x99n</span></span>/</a></span></span>), also known as <b>Devonshire</b>, which was formerly its common and official name, is a <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_England" title="Counties of England">county</a> of <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, reaching from the <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Channel" title="Bristol Channel">Bristol Channel</a> in the north to the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a> in the south. It is part of <a href="/wiki/South_West_England" title="South West England">South West England</a>, bounded by <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a> to the west, <a href="/wiki/Somerset" title="Somerset">Somerset</a> to the north east, and <a href="/wiki/Dorset" title="Dorset">Dorset</a> to the east. The city of <a href="/wiki/Exeter" title="Exeter">Exeter</a> is the <a href="/wiki/County_town" title="County town">county town</a>. The county includes the districts of <a href="/wiki/East_Devon" title="East Devon">East Devon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mid_Devon" title="Mid Devon">Mid Devon</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Devon" title="North Devon">North Devon</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Hams" title="South Hams">South Hams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Teignbridge" title="Teignbridge">Teignbridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Torridge" title="Torridge">Torridge</a>, and <a href="/wiki/West_Devon" title="West Devon">West Devon</a>. <a href="/wiki/Plymouth" title="Plymouth">Plymouth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Torbay" title="Torbay">Torbay</a> are each geographically part of Devon, but are administered as <a href="/wiki/Unitary_authorities" class="mw-redirect" title="Unitary authorities">unitary authorities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Combined as a <a href="/wiki/Ceremonial_counties_of_England" title="Ceremonial counties of England">ceremonial county</a>, Devon\'s area is 6,707&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (2,590 square miles)<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and its population is about 1.1 million.\n</p><p>Devon derives its name from <a href="/wiki/Dumnonia" title="Dumnonia">Dumnonia</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/British_Iron_Age" title="British Iron Age">British Iron Age</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Britain" title="Roman Britain">Roman Britain</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Sub-Roman_Britain" title="Sub-Roman Britain">early Middle Ages</a>, this was the homeland of the <a href="/wiki/Dumnonii" title="Dumnonii">Dumnonii</a> <a href="/wiki/Celtic_Britons" title="Celtic Britons">Brittonic</a> Celts. (The shift from "M" to "V" is a typical Celtic <a href="/wiki/Lenition" title="Lenition">consonant shift</a>.) The <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon_settlement_of_Britain" title="Anglo-Saxon settlement of Britain">Anglo-Saxon settlement of Britain</a> resulted in the partial assimilation of Dumnonia into the Kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Wessex" title="Wessex">Wessex</a> during the eighth and ninth centuries. The western boundary with Cornwall was set at the <a href="/wiki/River_Tamar" title="River Tamar">River Tamar</a> by <a href="/wiki/%C3%86thelstan" title="\xc3\x86thelstan">King \xc3\x86thelstan</a> in 936. Devon was later constituted as a <a href="/wiki/Shire" title="Shire">shire</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">Kingdom of England</a>.\n</p><p>The north and south coasts of Devon each have both cliffs and sandy shores, and the county\'s <a href="/wiki/Bay" title="Bay">bays</a> contain <a href="/wiki/Seaside_resort" title="Seaside resort">seaside resorts</a>, fishing towns, and ports. The inland terrain is rural and generally hilly, and has a lower population density than many other parts of England. <a href="/wiki/Dartmoor" title="Dartmoor">Dartmoor</a> is the largest open space in southern England, at 954&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (368 square miles);<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> its <a href="/wiki/Moorland" title="Moorland">moorland</a> extends across a large expanse of <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">granite</a> bedrock. To the north of Dartmoor are the <a href="/wiki/Culm_Measures" title="Culm Measures">Culm Measures</a> and <a href="/wiki/Exmoor" title="Exmoor">Exmoor</a>. In the valleys and lowlands of south and east Devon the soil is more fertile, drained by rivers including the <a href="/wiki/River_Exe" title="River Exe">Exe</a>, the <a href="/wiki/River_Culm" title="River Culm">Culm</a>, the <a href="/wiki/River_Teign" title="River Teign">Teign</a>, the <a href="/wiki/River_Dart" title="River Dart">Dart</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/River_Otter,_Devon" title="River Otter, Devon">Otter</a>.\n</p><p>As well as agriculture, much of the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Devon" title="Economy of Devon">economy of Devon</a> is based on <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a>. The comparatively mild climate, coastline and landscape make Devon a destination for <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_England" title="Tourism in England">recreation and leisure in England</a>, with visitors particularly attracted to the Dartmoor and Exmoor <a href="/wiki/National_Parks_in_England_and_Wales" class="mw-redirect" title="National Parks in England and Wales">national parks</a>; its coasts, including the resort towns along the south coast known collectively as the <a href="/wiki/English_Riviera" class="mw-redirect" title="English Riviera">English Riviera</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Jurassic_Coast" title="Jurassic Coast">Jurassic Coast</a>, and <a href="/wiki/North_Devon%27s_Biosphere_Reserve" title="North Devon&#39;s Biosphere Reserve">North Devon\'s UNESCO Biosphere Reserve</a>; and the countryside including the <a href="/wiki/Cornwall_and_West_Devon_Mining_Landscape" title="Cornwall and West Devon Mining Landscape">Cornwall and West Devon Mining Landscape</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-2"><a href="#Toponymy"><span class="tocnumber">1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Toponymy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3"><a href="#Human_occupation"><span class="tocnumber">1.2</span> <span class="toctext">Human occupation</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4"><a href="#Economy_and_industry"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Economy and industry</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5"><a href="#Transport"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Transport</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6"><a href="#Rail"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Rail</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-7"><a href="#Devon_Metro"><span class="tocnumber">3.1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Devon Metro</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8"><a href="#Air"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Air</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9"><a href="#Geography_and_geology"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Geography and geology</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#Geology"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Geology</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11"><a href="#Climate"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Climate</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#Ecology"><span class="tocnumber">4.3</span> <span class="toctext">Ecology</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#Politics_and_administration"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Politics and administration</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#Cities,_towns_and_villages"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Cities, towns and villages</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Religion"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Religion</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#Ancient_and_medieval_history"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Ancient and medieval history</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Later_history"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Later history</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Judaism"><span class="tocnumber">7.3</span> <span class="toctext">Judaism</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Symbols"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Symbols</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Coat_of_arms"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Coat of arms</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Flag"><span class="tocnumber">8.2</span> <span class="toctext">Flag</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#Place_names_and_customs"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Place names and customs</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#Education"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Education</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#Cuisine"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Cuisine</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#Sport"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Sport</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#Devonians"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Devonians</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Notable_people"><span class="tocnumber">13.1</span> <span class="toctext">Notable people</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">17</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">18</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Devon" title="History of Devon">History of Devon</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Toponymy">Toponymy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Toponymy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The name <i>Devon</i> derives from the name of the <a href="/wiki/Britons" class="mw-redirect" title="Britons">Britons</a> who inhabited the southwestern peninsula of Britain at the time of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_conquest_of_Britain" title="Roman conquest of Britain">Roman conquest of Britain</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/Dumnonii" title="Dumnonii">Dumnonii</a>, thought to mean "deep valley dwellers" from <a href="/wiki/Proto-Celtic_language" title="Proto-Celtic language">proto Celtic</a> <i>*dubnos</i> \'deep\'. In the <a href="/wiki/Brittonic_languages" title="Brittonic languages">Brittonic</a>, Devon is known as <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a>: <i lang="cy">Dyfnaint</i>, <a href="/wiki/Breton_language" title="Breton language">Breton</a>: <i lang="br">Devnent</i> and <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>: <i lang="kw">Dewnens</i>, each meaning "deep valleys." (For an account of Celtic <i><a href="/wiki/Dumnonia" title="Dumnonia">Dumnonia</a></i>, see the separate article.) Among the most common Devon placenames is <i>-combe</i> which derives from Brittonic <i>cwm</i> meaning \'valley\' usually prefixed by the name of the possessor.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/William_Camden" title="William Camden">William Camden</a>, in his 1607 edition of <i>Britannia</i>, described Devon as being one part of an older, wider country that once included Cornwall:\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>THAT region which, according to the Geographers, is the first of all Britaine, and, growing straiter still and narrower, shooteth out farthest into the West, [...] was in antient time inhabited by those Britans whom Solinus called Dumnonii, Ptolomee Damnonii [...] For their habitation all over this Countrey is somewhat low and in valleys, which manner of dwelling is called in the British tongue Dan-munith, in which sense also the Province next adjoyning in like respect is at this day named by the Britans Duffneit, that is to say, Low valleys. [...] But the Country of this nation is at this day divided into two parts, knowen by later names of Cornwall and Denshire, [...]</p><div class="templatequotecite">\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<cite>William Camden, <i>Britannia</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></cite></div>\n</blockquote>\n<p>The term "Devon" is normally used for everyday purposes e.g. "Devon County Council" but "Devonshire" continues to be used in the names of the "<a href="/wiki/Devonshire_and_Dorset_Regiment" title="Devonshire and Dorset Regiment">Devonshire and Dorset Regiment</a>" (until 2007) and "<a href="/wiki/The_Devonshire_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="The Devonshire Association">The Devonshire Association</a>". One erroneous theory is that the "shire" suffix is due to a mistake in the making of the original letters patent for the <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Devonshire#Earls_of_Devon" title="Duke of Devonshire">Duke of Devonshire</a>, resident in <a href="/wiki/Derbyshire" title="Derbyshire">Derbyshire</a>. However, there are references to "Defenascire" in <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Saxon">Anglo-Saxon</a> texts from before 1000 AD (this would mean "Shire of the Devonians"),<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> which translates to modern English as "Devonshire". The term Devonshire may have originated around the 8th century, when it changed from <i>Dumnonia</i> (<a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a>) to <i>Defenascir</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_occupation">Human occupation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Human occupation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Drizzlecombe_stones_6.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Drizzlecombe_stones_6.JPG/170px-Drizzlecombe_stones_6.JPG" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Drizzlecombe_stones_6.JPG/255px-Drizzlecombe_stones_6.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Drizzlecombe_stones_6.JPG/340px-Drizzlecombe_stones_6.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3056" data-file-height="4592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Drizzlecombe_stones_6.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Menhir" title="Menhir">Menhir</a> at <a href="/wiki/Drizzlecombe" title="Drizzlecombe">Drizzlecombe</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Kents_Cavern" title="Kents Cavern">Kents Cavern</a> in Torquay had produced human remains from 30\xe2\x80\x9340,000 years ago. <a href="/wiki/Dartmoor" title="Dartmoor">Dartmoor</a> is thought to have been occupied by <a href="/wiki/Mesolithic" title="Mesolithic">Mesolithic</a> <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherer</a> peoples from about 6000 BC. The Romans held the area under military occupation for around 350 years. Later, the area began to experience Saxon incursions from the east around 600 AD, firstly as small bands of settlers along the coasts of <a href="/wiki/Lyme_Bay" title="Lyme Bay">Lyme Bay</a> and southern estuaries and later as more organised bands pushing in from the east. Devon became a frontier between <a href="/wiki/Britons_(Celtic_people)" class="mw-redirect" title="Britons (Celtic people)">Brittonic</a>  and <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxons" title="Anglo-Saxons">Anglo-Saxon</a> <a href="/wiki/Wessex" title="Wessex">Wessex</a>, and it was largely absorbed into Wessex by the mid 9th century. A genetic study carried out by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">University of Oxford</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/University_College_London" title="University College London">University College London</a> discovered separate genetic groups in Cornwall and Devon, not only were there differences on either side of the Tamar, with a division almost exactly along the modern county boundary dating back to the 6th Century<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> but also between Devon and the rest of Southern England, and similarities with the modern northern <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Brittany" title="Brittany">Brittany</a>. This suggests the Anglo-Saxon migration into Devon was limited rather than a mass movement of people.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The border with Cornwall was set by King <a href="/wiki/%C3%86thelstan" title="\xc3\x86thelstan">\xc3\x86thelstan</a> on the east bank of the <a href="/wiki/River_Tamar" title="River Tamar">River Tamar</a> in 936 AD. Danish raids also occurred sporadically along many coastal parts of Devon between around 800AD and just before the time of the Norman conquest, including the silver mint at <i>Hlidaforda</i> <a href="/wiki/Lydford" title="Lydford">Lydford</a> in 997 and Taintona (a settlement on the <a href="/wiki/River_Teign" title="River Teign">Teign</a> estuary) in 1001.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Devon has also featured in most of the civil conflicts in England since the <a href="/wiki/Norman_conquest_of_England" title="Norman conquest of England">Norman conquest</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Wars_of_the_Roses" title="Wars of the Roses">Wars of the Roses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perkin_Warbeck" title="Perkin Warbeck">Perkin Warbeck</a>\'s rising in 1497, the <a href="/wiki/Prayer_Book_Rebellion" title="Prayer Book Rebellion">Prayer Book Rebellion</a> of 1549, and the <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">English Civil War</a>. The arrival of <a href="/wiki/William_III_of_England" title="William III of England">William of Orange</a> to launch the <a href="/wiki/Glorious_Revolution" title="Glorious Revolution">Glorious Revolution</a> of 1688 took place at <a href="/wiki/Brixham" title="Brixham">Brixham</a>.\n</p><p>Devon has produced <a href="/wiki/Tin" title="Tin">tin</a>, copper and other metals from ancient times. Devon\'s tin miners enjoyed a substantial degree of independence through Devon\'s <a href="/wiki/Stannary_Courts_and_Parliaments" class="mw-redirect" title="Stannary Courts and Parliaments">Stannary Parliament</a>, which dates back to the 12th century. The last recorded sitting was in 1748.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy_and_industry">Economy and industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Economy and industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Devon" title="Economy of Devon">Economy of Devon</a></div>\n<p>Like neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a> to the west, historically Devon has been disadvantaged economically compared to other parts of <a href="/wiki/Southern_England" title="Southern England">Southern England</a>, owing to the decline of a number of core industries, notably fishing, mining and farming. Agriculture has been an important industry in Devon since the 19th century. The <a href="/wiki/2001_United_Kingdom_foot-and-mouth_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="2001 United Kingdom foot-and-mouth crisis">2001 UK foot and mouth crisis</a> harmed the farming community severely.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Since then some parts of the agricultural industry have begun to diversify and recover, with a strong local food sector and many artisan producers. Nonetheless in 2015 the dairy industry was still suffering from the low prices offered for wholesale milk by major dairies and especially large supermarket chains.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Torquay.devon.750pix.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Torquay.devon.750pix.jpg/220px-Torquay.devon.750pix.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Torquay.devon.750pix.jpg/330px-Torquay.devon.750pix.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Torquay.devon.750pix.jpg/440px-Torquay.devon.750pix.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="563" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Torquay.devon.750pix.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Part of the seafront of <a href="/wiki/Torquay" title="Torquay">Torquay</a>, south Devon, at high tide.</div></div></div>\n<p>The attractive lifestyle of the area is drawing in new industries which are not heavily dependent upon geographical location;<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dartmoor" title="Dartmoor">Dartmoor</a>, for instance, has recently seen a significant rise in the percentage of its inhabitants involved in the financial services sector. The <a href="/wiki/Met_Office" title="Met Office">Met Office</a>, the UK\'s national and international weather service, moved to Exeter in 2003. Plymouth hosts the head office and first ever store of <a href="/wiki/The_Range_(retailer)" title="The Range (retailer)">The Range</a>, the only major national retail chain headquartered in Devon.\n</p><p>Since the rise of seaside resorts with the arrival of the railways in the 19th century, Devon\'s economy has been heavily reliant on tourism. The county\'s economy followed the declining trend of British seaside resorts since the mid-20th century, but with some recent revival and regeneration of its resorts, particularly focused around camping; sports such as surfing, cycling, sailing and heritage. This revival has been aided by the designation of much of Devon\'s countryside and coastline as the Dartmoor and <a href="/wiki/Exmoor" title="Exmoor">Exmoor</a> national parks, and the <a href="/wiki/Jurassic_Coast" title="Jurassic Coast">Jurassic Coast</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cornwall_and_West_Devon_Mining_Landscape" title="Cornwall and West Devon Mining Landscape">Cornwall and West Devon Mining Landscape</a> World Heritage Sites. In 2004 the county\'s tourist revenue was \xc2\xa31.2&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> More successful visitor attractions are particularly concentrated on food and drink, the South West Coast Path and watersports, including sea-view restaurants in North-West Devon (such as one example belonging to <a href="/wiki/Damien_Hurst" class="mw-redirect" title="Damien Hurst">Damien Hurst</a>); surfing there, indoor and outdoor folk music festivals across the county and sailing in the 5-mile (8.0&#160;km) hill-surrounded inlet (<a href="/wiki/Ria" title="Ria">ria</a>) at Salcombe.\n</p><p>Incomes vary significantly and the average is bolstered by a high proportion of affluent retired people from across Europe\'s major cities, particularly from the rest of England. Incomes in much of the South Hams and in villages surrounding Exeter and Plymouth are above the national average.  The claimant count of the unemployed and people receiving very low incomes is close to the national average of 4.5% in Torbay, Plymouth and Exeter. Their exurbs and rural villages contribute to low unemployment in the administrative county as shown below.\n</p><p>The table also shows the population change in the ten years to the 2011 census by subdivision.  It also shows the proportion of residents in each district reliant upon lowest income and/or joblessness benefits, the national average proportion of which was 4.5% as at August 2012, the year for which latest datasets have been published.  It can be seen that the most populous district of Devon is <a href="/wiki/East_Devon" title="East Devon">East Devon</a> but only if excluding <a href="/wiki/Torbay" title="Torbay">Torbay</a> which has marginally more residents and <a href="/wiki/Plymouth" title="Plymouth">Plymouth</a> which has approximately double the number of residents of either of these.  <a href="/wiki/West_Devon" title="West Devon">West Devon</a> has the fewest residents, having 63,839 at the time of the census.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption><i>Population from census to census. class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The key train operator for Devon is <a href="/wiki/Great_Western_Railway_(train_operating_company)" title="Great Western Railway (train operating company)">Great Western Railway</a>, which operates numerous regional, local and suburban services, as well as intercity services north to <a href="/wiki/Paddington_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Paddington railway station">London Paddington</a> and south to <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_railway_station" title="Plymouth railway station">Plymouth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Penzance_railway_station" title="Penzance railway station">Penzance</a>. Other intercity services are operated by <a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a> north to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Piccadilly_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Piccadilly railway station">Manchester Piccadilly</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Waverley_railway_station" title="Edinburgh Waverley railway station">Edinburgh Waverley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Central_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Glasgow Central railway station">Glasgow Central</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dundee_railway_station" title="Dundee railway station">Dundee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen_railway_station" title="Aberdeen railway station">Aberdeen</a> and south to Plymouth and Penzance, and <a href="/wiki/South_Western_Railway_(train_operating_company)" title="South Western Railway (train operating company)">South Western Railway</a>,operating services between <a href="/wiki/London_Waterloo_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="London Waterloo railway station">London Waterloo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Exeter_St_Davids_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Exeter St Davids railway station">Exeter St Davids</a> via the <a href="/wiki/West_of_England_Main_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="West of England Main Line">West of England Main Line</a>. All Devon services are diesel-hauled, since there are no electrified lines in the county.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Exeter_to_Plymouth_railway_of_the_LSWR" title="Exeter to Plymouth railway of the LSWR">Exeter to Plymouth railway of the LSWR</a> needs to be reopened to connect <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plymouth" title="Plymouth">Plymouth</a> to the rest of the UK railway system on an all weather basis. There are proposals to reopen the line from <a href="/wiki/Tavistock_railway_station" title="Tavistock railway station">Tavistock</a> to <a href="/wiki/Bere_Alston_railway_station" title="Bere Alston railway station">Bere Alston</a> for a through service to Plymouth.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> On the night of 4 February 2014, amid high winds and extremely rough seas, part of the <a href="/wiki/South_Devon_Railway_sea_wall" title="South Devon Railway sea wall">sea wall</a> at <a href="/wiki/Dawlish" title="Dawlish">Dawlish</a> was breached washing away around 40 metres (130&#160;ft) of the wall and the ballast under the railway immediately behind. The line was closed. <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail" title="Network Rail">Network Rail</a> began repair work <sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> and the line reopened on 4 April 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> In the wake of widespread disruption caused by damage to the mainline track at Dawlish by coastal storms in February 2014, Network Rail are considering reopening the Tavistock to <a href="/wiki/Okehampton_railway_station" title="Okehampton railway station">Okehampton</a> and Exeter section of the line as an alternative to the coastal route.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Devon_Metro">Devon Metro</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Devon Metro">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Devon County Council has proposed a "Devon Metro" scheme to improve rail services in the county and offer a realistic alternative to car travel. This includes the delivery of <a href="/wiki/Cranbrook_railway_station_(Devon)" title="Cranbrook railway station (Devon)">Cranbrook station</a>, plus four new stations (including <a href="/wiki/Edginswell_railway_station" title="Edginswell railway station">Edginswell</a>) as a priority.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Exeter_Airport" title="Exeter Airport">Exeter Airport</a> is a base for <a href="/wiki/Flybe" title="Flybe">Flybe</a>. Destinations include <a href="/wiki/London_City_Airport" title="London City Airport">London City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Airport" title="Dublin Airport">Dublin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport" title="Charles de Gaulle Airport">Paris</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Airport">Amsterdam</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_geology">Geography and geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Geography and geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Heath.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Heath.jpg/220px-Heath.jpg" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Heath.jpg/330px-Heath.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Heath.jpg/440px-Heath.jpg 2x" data-file-width="635" data-file-height="375" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Heath.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Heath_(habitat)" class="mw-redirect" title="Heath (habitat)">Heathland</a> at <a href="/wiki/Woodbury_Common,_Devon" title="Woodbury Common, Devon">Woodbury Common</a> in south east Devon.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Devon_Cliffs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Devon_Cliffs.jpg/220px-Devon_Cliffs.jpg" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Devon_Cliffs.jpg/330px-Devon_Cliffs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Devon_Cliffs.jpg/440px-Devon_Cliffs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Devon_Cliffs.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cliffs in Devon.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ilfracombe.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Ilfracombe.jpg/220px-Ilfracombe.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Ilfracombe.jpg/330px-Ilfracombe.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Ilfracombe.jpg/440px-Ilfracombe.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ilfracombe.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ilfracombe" title="Ilfracombe">Ilfracombe</a>, on the coast of <a href="/wiki/North_Devon" title="North Devon">North Devon</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Devon straddles <a href="/wiki/South_West_Peninsula" title="South West Peninsula">a peninsula</a> and so has two separate coastlines, on the <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Channel" title="Bristol Channel">Bristol Channel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Celtic_Sea" title="Celtic Sea">Celtic Sea</a> in the north, and on the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a> in the south.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/South_West_Coast_Path" title="South West Coast Path">South West Coast Path</a> runs along the entire length of both, around 65% of which is named as <a href="/wiki/Heritage_Coast" class="mw-redirect" title="Heritage Coast">Heritage Coast</a>. Before the changes to English counties in 1974, Devon was the <a href="/wiki/Historic_counties_of_England#List_of_counties" title="Historic counties of England">third largest county</a> by area and the largest of the counties not divided into county-like divisions (only Yorkshire and Lincolnshire were larger and both were sub-divided into ridings or parts, respectively).<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Since 1974 the county is ranked fourth by area (due to the creation of Cumbria) <a href="/wiki/List_of_ceremonial_counties_of_England" title="List of ceremonial counties of England">amongst ceremonial counties</a> and is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_two-tier_counties_of_England" title="List of two-tier counties of England">third largest non-metropolitan county</a>. The island of <a href="/wiki/Lundy" title="Lundy">Lundy</a> and the reef of <a href="/wiki/Eddystone_Rocks" title="Eddystone Rocks">Eddystone</a> are also in Devon. The county has more mileage of road than any other county in England.\n</p><p>Inland, the <a href="/wiki/Dartmoor" title="Dartmoor">Dartmoor</a> <a href="/wiki/National_park" title="National park">National Park</a> lies wholly in Devon, and the <a href="/wiki/Exmoor" title="Exmoor">Exmoor</a> National Park lies in both Devon and <a href="/wiki/Somerset" title="Somerset">Somerset</a>. Apart from these areas of high moorland the county has attractive rolling rural scenery and villages with <a href="/wiki/Thatch" class="mw-redirect" title="Thatch">thatched</a> <a href="/wiki/Cob_(building)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cob (building)">cob</a> cottages. All these features make Devon a popular <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">holiday</a> destination.\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/South_Devon" title="South Devon">South Devon</a> the landscape consists of rolling hills dotted with small towns, such as <a href="/wiki/Dartmouth,_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Dartmouth, England">Dartmouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivybridge" title="Ivybridge">Ivybridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingsbridge" title="Kingsbridge">Kingsbridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salcombe" title="Salcombe">Salcombe</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Totnes" title="Totnes">Totnes</a>. The towns of <a href="/wiki/Torquay" title="Torquay">Torquay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paignton" title="Paignton">Paignton</a> are the principal <a href="/wiki/Seaside_resort" title="Seaside resort">seaside resorts</a> on the south coast. East Devon has the first seaside resort to be developed in the county, <a href="/wiki/Exmouth,_Devon" class="mw-redirect" title="Exmouth, Devon">Exmouth</a> and the more upmarket Georgian town of <a href="/wiki/Sidmouth" title="Sidmouth">Sidmouth</a>, headquarters of the East Devon District Council. Exmouth marks the western end of the <a href="/wiki/Jurassic_Coast" title="Jurassic Coast">Jurassic Coast</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>. Another notable feature is the <a href="/wiki/Exeter_to_Plymouth_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Exeter to Plymouth Line">coastal railway line</a> between Newton Abbot and the Exe Estuary: the red sandstone cliffs and sea views are very dramatic and in the resorts railway line and beaches are very near.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Torquay_Palm_Trees.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Torquay_Palm_Trees.jpg/220px-Torquay_Palm_Trees.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Torquay_Palm_Trees.jpg/330px-Torquay_Palm_Trees.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Torquay_Palm_Trees.jpg/440px-Torquay_Palm_Trees.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1054" data-file-height="791" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Torquay_Palm_Trees.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Torquay sea front during Storm Emma - March 2018</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/North_Devon" title="North Devon">North Devon</a> is very rural with few major towns except <a href="/wiki/Barnstaple" title="Barnstaple">Barnstaple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Great_Torrington" title="Great Torrington">Great Torrington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bideford" title="Bideford">Bideford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ilfracombe" title="Ilfracombe">Ilfracombe</a>. Devon\'s Exmoor coast has the highest cliffs in southern Britain, culminating in the <a href="/wiki/Hangman_cliffs" title="Hangman cliffs">Great Hangman</a>, a 318&#160;m (1,043&#160;ft) "hog\'s-back" hill with an 250&#160;m (820&#160;ft) cliff-face, located near Combe Martin Bay.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Its sister cliff is the 218&#160;m (715&#160;ft) Little Hangman, which marks the western edge of coastal Exmoor. One of the features of the North Devon coast is that <a href="/wiki/Bideford_Bay" title="Bideford Bay">Bideford Bay</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Hartland_Point" title="Hartland Point">Hartland Point</a> peninsula are both west-facing, Atlantic facing coastlines; so that a combination of an off-shore (east) wind and an Atlantic swell produce excellent surfing conditions. The beaches of Bideford Bay (<a href="/wiki/Woolacombe" title="Woolacombe">Woolacombe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saunton" title="Saunton">Saunton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Westward_Ho!" title="Westward Ho!">Westward Ho!</a> and <a href="/wiki/Croyde" title="Croyde">Croyde</a>), along with parts of North Cornwall and South Wales, are the main centres of surfing in Britain.\n</p>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mountains_and_hills_of_Devon" class="mw-redirect" title="List of mountains and hills of Devon">List of mountains and hills of Devon</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Geologic_map_Wales_%26_SW_England_EN.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Geologic_map_Wales_%26_SW_England_EN.svg/220px-Geologic_map_Wales_%26_SW_England_EN.svg.png" width="220" height="192" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Geologic_map_Wales_%26_SW_England_EN.svg/330px-Geologic_map_Wales_%26_SW_England_EN.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Geologic_map_Wales_%26_SW_England_EN.svg/440px-Geologic_map_Wales_%26_SW_England_EN.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2220" data-file-height="1940" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Geologic_map_Wales_%26_SW_England_EN.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Geological map of Wales &amp; Southwest England.</div></div></div>\n<p>A geological dividing line cuts across Devon roughly along the line of the <a href="/wiki/Bristol_to_Exeter_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Bristol to Exeter Line">Bristol to Exeter Line</a> and the M5 motorway east of Tiverton and Exeter. It is a part of the <a href="/wiki/Tees-Exe_line" title="Tees-Exe line">Tees-Exe line</a> broadly dividing Britain into a southeastern lowland zone typified by gently dipping <a href="/wiki/Sedimentary_rock" title="Sedimentary rock">sedimentary rocks</a> and a northwestern upland zone typified by <a href="/wiki/Igneous_rock" title="Igneous rock">igneous rocks</a> and folded sedimentary and <a href="/wiki/Metamorphic_rock" title="Metamorphic rock">metamorphic rocks</a>.\n</p><p>The principal geological components of Devon are the <a href="/wiki/Devonian" title="Devonian">Devonian</a> (in north Devon, south west Devon and extending into Cornwall); the <a href="/wiki/Culm_Measures" title="Culm Measures">Culm Measures</a> (north western Devon also extending into north Cornwall); and the <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">granite</a> <a href="/wiki/Intrusion" class="mw-redirect" title="Intrusion">intrusion</a> of <a href="/wiki/Dartmoor" title="Dartmoor">Dartmoor</a> in central Devon, part of the <a href="/wiki/Cornubian_batholith" title="Cornubian batholith">Cornubian batholith</a> forming the \'spine\' of the southwestern peninsula. There are small remains of pre-Devonian rocks on the south Devon coast.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The oldest rocks which can be dated are those of the Devonian period which are approximately 395\xe2\x80\x93345 million years old. Sandstones and shales were deposited in North and South Devon beneath tropical seas. In shallower waters, limestone beds were laid down in the area now near Torquay and Plymouth.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\nThis geological period was named after Devon by <a href="/wiki/Roderick_Murchison" title="Roderick Murchison">Roderick Murchison</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adam_Sedgwick" title="Adam Sedgwick">Adam Sedgwick</a> in the 1840s and is the only British county whose name is used worldwide as a geological time period.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Devon\'s second major rock system<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> is the Culm Measures, a geological formation of the <a href="/wiki/Carboniferous" title="Carboniferous">Carboniferous</a> period that occurs principally in Devon and <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a>. The measures are so called either from the occasional presence of a soft, sooty coal, which is known in Devon as <i>culm</i>, or from the contortions commonly found in the beds.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> This formation stretches from <a href="/wiki/Bideford" title="Bideford">Bideford</a> to <a href="/wiki/Bude" title="Bude">Bude</a> in Cornwall, and contributes to a gentler, greener, more rounded landscape. It is also found on the western, north and eastern borders of Dartmoor.\n</p><p>The sedimentary rocks in more eastern parts of the county include <a href="/wiki/Permian" title="Permian">Permian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Triassic" title="Triassic">Triassic</a> sandstones (giving rise to east Devon\'s well known fertile red soils); Bunter <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pebble_beds&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Pebble beds (page does not exist)">pebble beds</a> around Budleigh Salterton and Woodbury Common and <a href="/wiki/Jurassic" title="Jurassic">Jurassic</a> rocks in the easternmost parts of Devon. Smaller outcrops of younger rocks also exist, such as Cretaceous <a href="/wiki/Chalk" title="Chalk">chalk</a> cliffs at Beer Head and gravels on Haldon, plus <a href="/wiki/Eocene" title="Eocene">Eocene</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oligocene" title="Oligocene">Oligocene</a> <a href="/wiki/Ball_clay" title="Ball clay">ball clay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lignite" title="Lignite">lignite</a> deposits in the Bovey Basin, formed around 50 million years ago under tropical forest conditions.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Dartmoor#Climate" title="Dartmoor">Dartmoor \xc2\xa7&#160;Climate</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_south-west_England" title="Climate of south-west England">climate of south-west England</a></div>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small><i>(March 2010)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Devon generally has a mild climate, heavily influenced by the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Current" title="North Atlantic Current">North Atlantic Drift</a>. In winter snow is relatively uncommon away from high land, although there are exceptions, such as the snowfalls of <a href="/wiki/February_2009_Great_Britain_and_Ireland_snowfall" title="February 2009 Great Britain and Ireland snowfall">February 2009</a>, <a href="/wiki/Winter_of_2010-2011_in_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Winter of 2010-2011 in Great Britain and Ireland">December 2010</a>, and March 2018. The county has warm summers with occasional hot spells and cool rainy periods. Winters are generally mild and the county often experiences some of the mildest winters in the world for its latitude, with average daily maximum temperatures in January approaching 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F). Rainfall varies significantly across the county, ranging from over 2,000&#160;mm (79&#160;in) on parts of Dartmoor, to around 750&#160;mm (30&#160;in) in the <a href="/wiki/Rain_shadow" title="Rain shadow">rain shadow</a> along the coast in southeastern Devon and around Exeter. Sunshine amounts also vary widely: the moors are generally cloudy, but the SE coast from Salcombe to Exmouth is one of the sunniest parts of the UK. With westerly or southwesterly winds and high pressure the area around Torbay and Teignmouth will often be very warm, with long sunny spells due to shelter by high ground (<a href="/wiki/Foehn_wind" title="Foehn wind">Foehn wind</a>).\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable collapsible" style="width:90%; text-align:center; font-size:90%; line-height: 1.2em; margin:auto;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="14">Climate data for Devon\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Month\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Jan\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Feb\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Mar\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Apr\n</th>\n<th scope="col">May\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Jun\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Jul\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Aug\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Sep\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Oct\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Nov\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Dec\n</th>\n<th scope="col" style="border-left-width:medium">Year\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="text-align: center;">\n<th scope="row" style="height: 16px;">Average high \xc2\xb0C (\xc2\xb0F)\n</th>\n<td style="background: #FFE6CE;
