style="text-align:center"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Devon_fields_stitch.jpg" title="File:Devon fields stitch.jpg"> </a></div>Fields in south Devon after a snowfall.</div>\n</div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">Ecology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Ecology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pnies5.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Pnies5.jpg/220px-Pnies5.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Pnies5.jpg/330px-Pnies5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Pnies5.jpg/440px-Pnies5.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="602" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pnies5.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ponies grazing on Exmoor near <a href="/wiki/Brendon" title="Brendon">Brendon</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Devon" title="North Devon">North Devon</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The variety of habitats means that there is a wide range of wildlife (see <a href="/wiki/Dartmoor_wildlife" class="mw-redirect" title="Dartmoor wildlife">Dartmoor wildlife</a>, for example). A popular challenge among <a href="/wiki/Bird-watching" class="mw-redirect" title="Bird-watching">birders</a> is to find over 100 species in the county in a day.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The county\'s wildlife is protected by several wildlife charities such as the <a href="/wiki/Devon_Wildlife_Trust" title="Devon Wildlife Trust">Devon Wildlife Trust</a>, which looks after 40 nature reserves. The Devon Bird Watching and Preservation Society (founded in 1928 and known since 2005 as "Devon Birds") is a county bird society dedicated to the study and conservation of wild birds.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/RSPB" class="mw-redirect" title="RSPB">RSPB</a> has reserves in the county, and <a href="/wiki/Natural_England" title="Natural England">Natural England</a> is responsible for over 200 Devon <a href="/wiki/Sites_of_Special_Scientific_Interest" class="mw-redirect" title="Sites of Special Scientific Interest">Sites of Special Scientific Interest</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_nature_reserves_in_England" title="National nature reserves in England">National Nature Reserves</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> such as <a href="/wiki/Slapton_Ley" title="Slapton Ley">Slapton Ley</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Devon_Bat_Group" title="Devon Bat Group">Devon Bat Group</a> was founded in 1984 to help conserve bats.  Wildlife found in this area extend to a plethora of different kinds of insects, butterflies and moths; an interesting butterfly to take look at is the <a href="/wiki/Chequered_skipper" title="Chequered skipper">Chequered skipper</a>.\n</p><p>The botany of the county is very diverse and includes some rare species not found elsewhere in the British Isles other than Cornwall. Devon is divided into two <a href="/wiki/Watsonian_vice-counties" class="mw-redirect" title="Watsonian vice-counties">Watsonian vice-counties</a>: north and south, the boundary being an irregular line approximately across the higher part of Dartmoor and then along the canal eastwards. Botanical reports begin in the 17th century and there is a <i>Flora Devoniensis</i> by Jones and Kingston in 1829.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> A general account appeared in <i><a href="/wiki/Victoria_County_History#Dormant_counties" title="Victoria County History">The Victoria History of the County of Devon</a></i> (1906), and a <i>Flora of Devon</i> was published in 1939 by <a href="/wiki/William_Keble_Martin" title="William Keble Martin">Keble Martin</a> and Fraser.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> An <i>Atlas of the Devon Flora</i> by Ivimey-Cook appeared in 1984, and <i>A New Flora of Devon</i>, based on field work undertaken between 2005 and 2014, was published in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rising temperatures have led to Devon becoming the first place in modern Britain to cultivate <a href="/wiki/Olive" title="Olive">olives</a> commercially.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_administration">Politics and administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Politics and administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Devon_County_Council_election,_2013" title="Devon County Council election, 2013">Devon County Council election, 2013</a> and <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_2010" title="Local Government Act 2010">Local Government Act 2010</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Clock_tower,_County_Hall,_Exeter.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Clock_tower%2C_County_Hall%2C_Exeter.jpg/220px-Clock_tower%2C_County_Hall%2C_Exeter.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Clock_tower%2C_County_Hall%2C_Exeter.jpg/330px-Clock_tower%2C_County_Hall%2C_Exeter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Clock_tower%2C_County_Hall%2C_Exeter.jpg/440px-Clock_tower%2C_County_Hall%2C_Exeter.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Clock_tower,_County_Hall,_Exeter.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>County Hall, Exeter. Headquarters for Devon County Council.</div></div></div>\n<p>The administrative centre and capital of Devon is the city of <a href="/wiki/Exeter" title="Exeter">Exeter</a>. The largest city in Devon, <a href="/wiki/Plymouth" title="Plymouth">Plymouth</a>, and the conurbation of <a href="/wiki/Torbay" title="Torbay">Torbay</a> (which includes the largest town in Devon and capital of Torbay, <a href="/wiki/Torquay" title="Torquay">Torquay</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Paignton" title="Paignton">Paignton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brixham" title="Brixham">Brixham</a>) have been <a href="/wiki/Unitary_authorities_of_England" title="Unitary authorities of England">unitary authorities</a> since 1998, separate from the remainder of Devon which is administered by <a href="/wiki/Devon_County_Council" title="Devon County Council">Devon County Council</a> for the purposes of local government.\n</p><p>Devon County Council is controlled by the Conservatives, and the political representation of its 62 councillors are: 38 <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservatives</a>, 9 <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a>, seven <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a>, four <a href="/wiki/UK_Independence_Party" title="UK Independence Party">UKIP</a>, three <a href="/wiki/Independent_(politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Independent (politician)">Independents</a> and one <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales" title="Green Party of England and Wales">Green</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2015" title="United Kingdom general election, 2015">2015 general election</a>, Devon returned 11 Conservatives and one Labour MP from its <a href="/wiki/List_of_Parliamentary_constituencies_in_Devon" title="List of Parliamentary constituencies in Devon">12 constituencies</a> through first-past-the-post. The county is represented in the wider <a href="/wiki/South_West_England_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="South West England (European Parliament constituency)">South West England (European Parliament constituency)</a>, which returned two UKIP, two Conservative, one Labour and one Green <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">MEP</a> at the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2014_(United_Kingdom)" title="European Parliament election, 2014 (United Kingdom)">2014 election</a> using the <a href="/wiki/D%27Hondt_method" title="D&#39;Hondt method">d\'Hondt method</a> of <a href="/wiki/Party-list_proportional_representation" title="Party-list proportional representation">party-list proportional representation</a>.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Hundreds</dt></dl>\n<p>Historically Devon was divided into 32 <a href="/wiki/Hundred_(county_subdivision)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hundred (county subdivision)">hundreds</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Axminster_Hundred" title="Axminster Hundred">Axminster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bampton_Hundred" title="Bampton Hundred">Bampton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black_Torrington_Hundred" title="Black Torrington Hundred">Black Torrington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Braunton_Hundred" title="Braunton Hundred">Braunton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cliston_Hundred" title="Cliston Hundred">Cliston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coleridge_Hundred" title="Coleridge Hundred">Coleridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colyton_Hundred" title="Colyton Hundred">Colyton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crediton_Hundred" title="Crediton Hundred">Crediton</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Budleigh_Hundred" title="East Budleigh Hundred">East Budleigh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ermington_Hundred" title="Ermington Hundred">Ermington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Exminster_Hundred" title="Exminster Hundred">Exminster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fremington_Hundred" title="Fremington Hundred">Fremington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Halberton_Hundred" title="Halberton Hundred">Halberton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hartland_Hundred" title="Hartland Hundred">Hartland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hayridge_Hundred" title="Hayridge Hundred">Hayridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haytor_Hundred" title="Haytor Hundred">Haytor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hemyock_Hundred" title="Hemyock Hundred">Hemyock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lifton_Hundred" title="Lifton Hundred">Lifton</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Tawton_and_Winkleigh_Hundred" title="North Tawton and Winkleigh Hundred">North Tawton and Winkleigh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ottery_Hundred" title="Ottery Hundred">Ottery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plympton_Hundred" title="Plympton Hundred">Plympton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roborough_Hundred" title="Roborough Hundred">Roborough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shebbear_Hundred" title="Shebbear Hundred">Shebbear</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shirwell_Hundred" title="Shirwell Hundred">Shirwell</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Molton_Hundred" title="South Molton Hundred">South Molton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stanborough_Hundred" title="Stanborough Hundred">Stanborough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tavistock_Hundred" title="Tavistock Hundred">Tavistock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Teignbridge_Hundred" title="Teignbridge Hundred">Teignbridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tiverton_Hundred" title="Tiverton Hundred">Tiverton</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Budleigh_Hundred" title="West Budleigh Hundred">West Budleigh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Witheridge_Hundred" title="Witheridge Hundred">Witheridge</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wonford_Hundred" title="Wonford Hundred">Wonford</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Cities.2C_towns_and_villages"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Cities,_towns_and_villages">Cities, towns and villages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Cities, towns and villages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_places_in_Devon" title="List of places in Devon">List of places in Devon</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_towns_and_cities_in_Devon_by_population" title="List of towns and cities in Devon by population">List of towns and cities in Devon by population</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Devon.brixham.750pix.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Devon.brixham.750pix.jpg/220px-Devon.brixham.750pix.jpg" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Devon.brixham.750pix.jpg/330px-Devon.brixham.750pix.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Devon.brixham.750pix.jpg/440px-Devon.brixham.750pix.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="481" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Devon.brixham.750pix.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The inner harbour, <a href="/wiki/Brixham" title="Brixham">Brixham</a>, south Devon, at low tide.</div></div></div>\n<p>The main settlements in Devon are the cities of <a href="/wiki/Plymouth" title="Plymouth">Plymouth</a>, a historic port now administratively independent, <a href="/wiki/Exeter" title="Exeter">Exeter</a>, the <a href="/wiki/County_town" title="County town">county town</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Torbay" title="Torbay">Torbay</a>, the county\'s tourist centre. Devon\'s coast is lined with tourist resorts, many of which grew rapidly with the arrival of the railways in the 19th century. Examples include <a href="/wiki/Dawlish" title="Dawlish">Dawlish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Exmouth,_Devon" class="mw-redirect" title="Exmouth, Devon">Exmouth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sidmouth" title="Sidmouth">Sidmouth</a> on the south coast, and <a href="/wiki/Ilfracombe" title="Ilfracombe">Ilfracombe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lynmouth" title="Lynmouth">Lynmouth</a> on the north. The Torbay conurbation of <a href="/wiki/Torquay" title="Torquay">Torquay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paignton" title="Paignton">Paignton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brixham" title="Brixham">Brixham</a> on the south coast is now administratively independent of the county. Rural <a href="/wiki/Market_town" title="Market town">market towns</a> in the county include <a href="/wiki/Barnstaple" title="Barnstaple">Barnstaple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bideford" title="Bideford">Bideford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Honiton" title="Honiton">Honiton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newton_Abbot" title="Newton Abbot">Newton Abbot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Okehampton" title="Okehampton">Okehampton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tavistock,_Devon" class="mw-redirect" title="Tavistock, Devon">Tavistock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Totnes" title="Totnes">Totnes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tiverton,_Devon" title="Tiverton, Devon">Tiverton</a>.\n</p><p>The boundary with Cornwall has not always been on the River Tamar as at present: until the late 19th century a few parishes in the Torpoint area were in Devon and five parishes now in north-east Cornwall were in Devon until 1974. (However, for ecclesiastical purposes these were nevertheless in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Archdeacons_of_Cornwall" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Archdeacons of Cornwall">Archdeaconry of Cornwall</a> and in 1876 became part of the <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Truro" title="Diocese of Truro">Diocese of Truro</a>.)\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_and_medieval_history">Ancient and medieval history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Ancient and medieval history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small><i>(June 2017)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The region of Devon was the dominion of the Dumnonii <a href="/wiki/List_of_Celtic_tribes" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Celtic tribes">Celtic tribe</a> they were also called "Deep Valley Dwellers". The region was less Romanised than the rest of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Britain" title="Roman Britain">Roman Britain</a> since it was considered a remote province. The Romans left the region around AD 410, this is when one of the leading Dumnonii families attempted to create a dynasty and rules over Devon as the Kings of Dumnonii.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Celtic_polytheism" title="Celtic polytheism">Celtic paganism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_ancient_Rome" title="Religion in ancient Rome">Roman practices</a> were the first known religions in Devon, although in the mid-fourth century AD, Christianity was introduced to Devon.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Sub-Roman_Britain" title="Sub-Roman Britain">Sub-Roman period</a> the church in the British Isles was characterised by some differences in practice from the Latin Christianity of the continent of Europe and is known as <a href="/wiki/Celtic_Christianity" title="Celtic Christianity">Celtic Christianity</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> however it was always in communion with the wider Roman Catholic Church. Many <a href="/wiki/List_of_Cornish_saints" title="List of Cornish saints">Cornish saints</a> are commemorated also in Devon in legends, churches and placenames. <a href="/wiki/Western_Christianity" title="Western Christianity">Western Christianity</a> came to Devon when it was over a long period incorporated into the kingdom of Wessex and the jurisdiction of the bishop of Wessex. <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petroc" title="Saint Petroc">Saint Petroc</a> is said to have passed through Devon, where ancient dedications to him are even more numerous than in Cornwall: a probable seventeen (plus <a href="/wiki/Timberscombe" title="Timberscombe">Timberscombe</a> just over the border in Somerset), compared to Cornwall\'s five. The position of churches bearing his name, including one within the old Roman walls of <a href="/wiki/Exeter" title="Exeter">Exeter</a>, are nearly always near the coast, reminding us that in those days travelling was done mainly by sea. The Devonian villages of <a href="/wiki/Petrockstowe" title="Petrockstowe">Petrockstowe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Newton_St_Petroc" class="mw-redirect" title="Newton St Petroc">Newton St Petroc</a> are also named after Saint Petroc and the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Devon" title="Flag of Devon">flag of Devon</a> is dedicated to him.\n</p><p>The history of Christianity in the South West of England remains to some degree obscure. Parts of the historic county of Devon formed part of the diocese of Wessex, while nothing is known of the church organisation of the Celtic areas. About 703 Devon and Cornwall were included in the separate diocese of Sherborne and in 900 this was again divided into two, the Devon bishop having from 905 his seat at Tawton (now <a href="/wiki/Bishop%27s_Tawton" title="Bishop&#39;s Tawton">Bishop\'s Tawton</a>) and from 912 at <a href="/wiki/Crediton" title="Crediton">Crediton</a>, birthplace of St Boniface. <a href="/wiki/Lyfing,_Abbot_of_Tavistock" class="mw-redirect" title="Lyfing, Abbot of Tavistock">Lyfing</a> became <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Crediton" title="Bishop of Crediton">Bishop of Crediton</a> in 1027 and shortly afterwards became <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Cornwall" title="Bishop of Cornwall">Bishop of Cornwall</a>.\n</p><p>The two dioceses of Crediton and Cornwall, covering Devon and Cornwall, were permanently united under <a href="/wiki/Edward_the_Confessor" title="Edward the Confessor">Edward the Confessor</a> by <a href="/wiki/Lyfing,_Abbot_of_Tavistock" class="mw-redirect" title="Lyfing, Abbot of Tavistock">Lyfing</a>\'s successor <a href="/wiki/Leofric,_Bishop_of_Exeter" class="mw-redirect" title="Leofric, Bishop of Exeter">Bishop Leofric</a>, hitherto Bishop of Crediton, who became first Bishop of Exeter under <a href="/wiki/Edward_the_Confessor" title="Edward the Confessor">Edward the Confessor</a>, which was established as his cathedral city in 1050. At first, the abbey church of St Mary and St Peter, founded by Athelstan in 932 and rebuilt in 1019, served as the cathedral.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_history">Later history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Later history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1549, the <a href="/wiki/Prayer_Book_Rebellion" title="Prayer Book Rebellion">Prayer Book Rebellion</a> caused the deaths of thousands of people from Devon and Cornwall. During the <a href="/wiki/English_Reformation" title="English Reformation">English Reformation</a>, churches in Devon officially became affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a>. From the late sixteenth century onwards, zealous Protestantism \xe2\x80\x93 or \'puritanism\' \xe2\x80\x93 became increasingly well-entrenched in some parts of Devon, while other districts of the county remained much more conservative. These divisions would become starkly apparent during the English Civil War of 1642\xe2\x80\x9346, when the county split apart along religious and cultural lines.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Methodism" title="Methodism">Methodism</a> of <a href="/wiki/John_Wesley" title="John Wesley">John Wesley</a> proved to be very popular with the working classes in Devon in the 19th century. Methodist chapels became important social centres, with male voice choirs and other church-affiliated groups playing a central role in the social lives of working class Devonians. Methodism still plays a large part in the religious life of Devon today, although the county has shared in the post-World War II decline in British religious feeling.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Exeter" title="Diocese of Exeter">Diocese of Exeter</a> remains the Anglican diocese including the whole of Devon. The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Plymouth" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Plymouth">Roman Catholic Diocese of Plymouth</a> was established in the mid 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judaism">Judaism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Judaism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Despite its small Jewish population, Devon is also noted for containing two of Britain\'s oldest synagogues, located in <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Synagogue" title="Plymouth Synagogue">Plymouth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Exeter_Synagogue" title="Exeter Synagogue">Exeter</a>, built in 1762 and 1763 respectively.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Symbols">Symbols</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Symbols">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Coat of arms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Devon_arms.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Devon_arms.png/220px-Devon_arms.png" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Devon_arms.png/330px-Devon_arms.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Devon_arms.png/440px-Devon_arms.png 2x" data-file-width="658" data-file-height="500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Devon_arms.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a> of Devon County Council.</div></div></div>\n<p>There was no established <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a> for the county until 1926: the arms of the City of <a href="/wiki/Exeter" title="Exeter">Exeter</a> were often used to represent Devon, for instance in the badge of the <a href="/wiki/Devonshire_Regiment" title="Devonshire Regiment">Devonshire Regiment</a>. During the forming of a county council by the <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_1888" title="Local Government Act 1888">Local Government Act 1888</a> adoption of a common seal was required. The seal contained three shields depicting the arms of Exeter along with those of the first chairman and vice-chairman of the council (<a href="/wiki/Charles_Hepburn-Stuart-Forbes-Trefusis,_20th_Baron_Clinton" title="Charles Hepburn-Stuart-Forbes-Trefusis, 20th Baron Clinton">Lord Clinton</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Morley" title="Earl of Morley">Earl of Morley</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 11 October 1926, the county council received a grant of arms from the <a href="/wiki/College_of_Arms" title="College of Arms">College of Arms</a>. The main part of the shield displays a red crowned lion on a silver field, the arms of <a href="/wiki/Richard,_Earl_of_Cornwall" class="mw-redirect" title="Richard, Earl of Cornwall">Richard Plantagenet, Earl of Cornwall</a>. The <i>chief</i> or upper portion of the shield depicts an ancient ship on wavers, for Devon\'s seafaring traditions. The <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> motto adopted was <i>Auxilio Divino</i> (by Divine aid), that of Sir <a href="/wiki/Francis_Drake" title="Francis Drake">Francis Drake</a>. The 1926 grant was of arms alone. On 6 March 1962 a further grant of crest and supporters was obtained. The crest is the head of a <a href="/wiki/Dartmoor_Pony" class="mw-redirect" title="Dartmoor Pony">Dartmoor Pony</a> rising from a "Naval Crown". This distinctive form of crown is formed from the sails and sterns of ships, and is associated with the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>. The supporters are a <a href="/wiki/North_Devon_cattle" title="North Devon cattle">Devon bull</a> and a sea lion.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Devon_County_Council" title="Devon County Council">Devon County Council</a> adopted a "ship silhouette" logo after the 1974 reorganisation, adapted from the ship emblem on the coat of arms, but following the loss in 1998 of Plymouth and Torbay re-adopted the coat of arms. In April 2006 the council unveiled a new logo which was to be used in most everyday applications, though the coat of arms will continue to be used for "various civic purposes".<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flag">Flag</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Flag">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Devon" title="Flag of Devon">Flag of Devon</a></div>\n<p>Devon also has its own flag which has been dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petroc" title="Saint Petroc">Saint Petroc</a>, a local <a href="/wiki/Saint" title="Saint">saint</a> with dedications throughout Devon and neighbouring counties. The flag was adopted in 2003 after a competition run by <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Devon" title="BBC Radio Devon">BBC Radio Devon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The winning design was created by website contributor Ryan Sealey, and won 49% of the votes cast. The colours of the flag are those popularly identified with Devon, for example, the colours of <a href="/wiki/Exeter_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Exeter University">Exeter University</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a> team, and the Green and White flag flown by the first <a href="/wiki/Viscount_Exmouth" title="Viscount Exmouth">Viscount Exmouth</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Bombardment_of_Algiers_(1816)" title="Bombardment of Algiers (1816)">Bombardment of Algiers</a> (now on view at the Teign Valley Museum), as well as one of the county\'s <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> teams, <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Argyle_F.C." title="Plymouth Argyle F.C.">Plymouth Argyle</a>. On 17 October 2006, the flag was hoisted for the first time outside County Hall in Exeter to mark Local Democracy Week, receiving official recognition from the county council.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Place_names_and_customs">Place names and customs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Place names and customs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Westwardho.beach.arp.750pix.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Westwardho.beach.arp.750pix.jpg/220px-Westwardho.beach.arp.750pix.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Westwardho.beach.arp.750pix.jpg/330px-Westwardho.beach.arp.750pix.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Westwardho.beach.arp.750pix.jpg/440px-Westwardho.beach.arp.750pix.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="561" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Westwardho.beach.arp.750pix.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The beach at <a href="/wiki/Westward_Ho!" title="Westward Ho!">Westward Ho!</a>, North Devon, looking north towards the shared <a href="/wiki/Estuary" title="Estuary">estuary</a> of the rivers <a href="/wiki/River_Taw" title="River Taw">Taw</a> and <a href="/wiki/River_Torridge" title="River Torridge">Torridge</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Devon\'s toponyms include many with the endings "coombe/combe" and "tor".  Both \'coombe\' (valley or hollow, cf. Welsh <i>cwm</i>, Cornish <i>komm</i>) and \'tor\' (Old Welsh <i>twrr</i> and Scots Gaelic <i>t\xc3\xb2rr</i> from Latin <i>turris</i>; \'tower\' used for granite formations) are rare  <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_words_of_Welsh_origin" title="List of English words of Welsh origin">Celtic loanwords in English</a> and their frequency is greatest in Devon which shares a boundary with <a href="/wiki/Brittonic_languages" title="Brittonic languages">Brittonic</a> speaking Cornwall.  Ruined medieval settlements of <a href="/wiki/Dartmoor_longhouse" title="Dartmoor longhouse">Dartmoor longhouses</a> indicate that dispersed rural settlement (OE <i>tun</i>, now often -ton) was very similar to that found in Cornish \'tre-\' settlements, however these are generally described with the local placename -(a)cott, from the Old English for homestead, cf. <a href="/wiki/Cottage" title="Cottage">cottage</a>. Saxon endings in -worthy (from Anglo-Saxon <i>worthig</i>) indicate larger settlements.  Several \'Bere\'s indicate Anglo-Saxon wood groves, as \'leighs\' indicate clearings.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Devon has a variety of festivals and traditional practices, including the traditional orchard-visiting <a href="/wiki/Wassail" title="Wassail">Wassail</a> in <a href="/wiki/Whimple" title="Whimple">Whimple</a> every 17 January, and the carrying of flaming tar barrels in <a href="/wiki/Ottery_St._Mary" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottery St. Mary">Ottery St. Mary</a>, where people who have lived in Ottery for long enough are called upon to celebrate <a href="/wiki/Guy_Fawkes_Night" title="Guy Fawkes Night">Bonfire Night</a> by running through the village (and the gathered crowds) with flaming barrels on their backs.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Berry_Pomeroy" title="Berry Pomeroy">Berry Pomeroy</a> still celebrates "Queen\'s Day" for <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Elizabeth I">Elizabeth I</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Devon" title="List of schools in Devon">List of schools in Devon</a></div>\n<p>Devon has a mostly <a href="/wiki/Comprehensive_education" class="mw-redirect" title="Comprehensive education">comprehensive education</a> system. There are 37 state and 23 independent secondary schools. There are three tertiary (<a href="/wiki/Further_education" title="Further education">FE</a>) colleges and an <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_college" class="mw-redirect" title="Agricultural college">agricultural college</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bicton_College" title="Bicton College">Bicton College</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Budleigh_Salterton" title="Budleigh Salterton">Budleigh Salterton</a>). Torbay has 8 state (with 3 <a href="/wiki/Grammar_school" title="Grammar school">grammar schools</a>) and 3 independent secondary schools, and Plymouth has 17 state (with 3 grammar schools \xe2\x80\x93 two female and one male) and one independent school, <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_College" title="Plymouth College">Plymouth College</a>. East Devon and Teignbridge have the largest school populations, with West Devon the smallest (with only two schools). Only one school in Exeter, Mid Devon, Torridge and North Devon have a <a href="/wiki/Sixth_form" title="Sixth form">sixth form</a> \xe2\x80\x93 the schools in other districts mostly have sixth forms, with all schools in West Devon and East Devon having a sixth form.\n</p><p>Two universities are located in Devon, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Exeter" title="University of Exeter">University of Exeter</a> (split between the <a href="/wiki/Streatham_Campus" title="Streatham Campus">Streatham Campus</a> and <a href="/wiki/St_Luke%27s_Campus" title="St Luke&#39;s Campus">St Luke\'s Campus</a>, both in Exeter, and a campus in <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a>); in Plymouth the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Plymouth" title="University of Plymouth">University of Plymouth</a> in Britain is present, along with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_St_Mark_%26_St_John" class="mw-redirect" title="University of St Mark &amp; St John">University of St Mark &amp; St John</a> to the city\'s north. The universities of Exeter and Plymouth have together formed the <a href="/wiki/Peninsula_College_of_Medicine_and_Dentistry" title="Peninsula College of Medicine and Dentistry">Peninsula College of Medicine and Dentistry</a> which has bases in Exeter and Plymouth. There is also <a href="/wiki/Schumacher_College" title="Schumacher College">Schumacher College</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Devon" title="Cuisine of Devon">Cuisine of Devon</a></div>\n<p>The county has given its name to a number of culinary specialities. The Devonshire <a href="/wiki/Cream_tea" title="Cream tea">cream tea</a>, involving <a href="/wiki/Scone_(bread)" class="mw-redirect" title="Scone (bread)">scones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jam" class="mw-redirect" title="Jam">jam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clotted_cream" title="Clotted cream">clotted cream</a>, is thought to have originated in Devon (though claims have also been made for neighbouring counties); in other countries, such as Australia and New Zealand, it is known as a "Devonshire tea".<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> In Australia, <a href="/wiki/Devon_(sausage)" title="Devon (sausage)">Devon</a> is a name for luncheon meat (processed ham).\n</p><p>In October 2008, Devon was awarded Fairtrade County status by the <a href="/wiki/Fairtrade_Foundation" class="mw-redirect" title="Fairtrade Foundation">Fairtrade Foundation</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Devon has been home to a number of customs, such as its own form of <a href="/wiki/Devon_wrestling" title="Devon wrestling">Devon wrestling</a>, similar in some ways to <a href="/wiki/Cornish_wrestling" title="Cornish wrestling">Cornish wrestling</a>. As recently as the 19th century, a crowd of 17,000 at Devonport, near <a href="/wiki/Plymouth" title="Plymouth">Plymouth</a>, attended a match between the champions of Devon and Cornwall. Another Devon sport was <a href="/wiki/Cornish_hurling" title="Cornish hurling">outhurling</a> which was played in some regions until the 20th century (e.g. 1922, at Great Torrington). Other ancient customs which survive include <a href="/wiki/Dartmoor" title="Dartmoor">Dartmoor</a> step dancing, and "<a href="/wiki/Crying_The_Neck" class="mw-redirect" title="Crying The Neck">Crying The Neck</a>".\n</p><p>Devon has three professional football teams, based in each of its most populous towns and cities. As of the <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_in_English_football" title="2017\xe2\x80\x9318 in English football">2017/2018 football season</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Argyle_F.C." title="Plymouth Argyle F.C.">Plymouth Argyle F.C.</a> compete in <a href="/wiki/Football_League_One" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League One">English Football League One</a> (the third tier of English professional football), <a href="/wiki/Exeter_City_F.C." title="Exeter City F.C.">Exeter City F.C.</a> compete in <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Two" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Two">English Football League Two</a> (the fourth tier), while <a href="/wiki/Torquay_United_F.C." title="Torquay United F.C.">Torquay United F.C.</a> compete in the <a href="/wiki/Conference_Premier" class="mw-redirect" title="Conference Premier">National League</a> (the fifth tier).   Plymouth\'s highest Football League finish was fourth in the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Second_Division" title="Football League Second Division">Second Division</a>, which was achieved twice, in 1932 and 1953.   Torquay and Exeter have never progressed beyond the third tier of the league; Torquay finished second on <a href="/wiki/Goal_average" class="mw-redirect" title="Goal average">goal average</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Third_Division" title="Football League Third Division">Third Division (S)</a> behind Sir <a href="/wiki/Alf_Ramsey" title="Alf Ramsey">Alf Ramsey</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Ipswich_Town_F.C." title="Ipswich Town F.C.">Ipswich Town</a> in 1957.  Exeter\'s highest position has been eighth in the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Third_Division" title="Football League Third Division">Third Division (S)</a>.  The county\'s biggest non-league clubs are <a href="/wiki/Bideford_F.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Bideford F.C.">Bideford F.C.</a> which competes in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Football_League_Premier_Division" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern Football League Premier Division">Southern Football League Premier Division</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tiverton_Town_F.C." title="Tiverton Town F.C.">Tiverton Town F.C.</a> which is in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Football_League_Division_One_South_and_West" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern Football League Division One South and West">Southern Football League Division One South and West</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Rugby_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Rugby Union">Rugby Union</a> is very popular in Devon with over forty clubs under the banner of the <a href="/wiki/Devon_Rugby_Football_Union" title="Devon Rugby Football Union">Devon Rugby Football Union</a>, many with numerous teams at senior, youth and junior levels. One club \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Exeter_Chiefs" title="Exeter Chiefs">Exeter Chiefs</a> play in the <a href="/wiki/English_Premiership_(rugby_union)" class="mw-redirect" title="English Premiership (rugby union)">Aviva Premiership</a>, winning the title in 2017 for the first time in their history after beating <a href="/wiki/Wasps_RFC" title="Wasps RFC">Wasps RFC</a> in the final 23-20. <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Albion_R.F.C." title="Plymouth Albion R.F.C.">Plymouth Albion</a> who are, as of  2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, in the <a href="/wiki/National_League_1" title="National League 1">National League 1</a> (The 3rd tier of English Professional Rugby Union.\nIn basketball, <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Raiders" title="Plymouth Raiders">Plymouth Raiders</a> play in the <a href="/wiki/British_Basketball_League" title="British Basketball League">British Basketball League</a>. <a href="/wiki/Tamar_Valley_Cannons" class="mw-redirect" title="Tamar Valley Cannons">Tamar Valley Cannons</a>, also based in Plymouth, are Devon\'s only other representatives in the National Leagues. <a href="/wiki/Motorcycle_speedway" title="Motorcycle speedway">Motorcycle speedway</a> is also supported in the county, with both the <a href="/wiki/Exeter_Falcons" title="Exeter Falcons">Exeter Falcons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Devils" title="Plymouth Devils">Plymouth Devils</a> succeeding in the National Leagues in recent years.\n</p><p>There are five <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> teams in Devon. <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_R.L.F.C" class="mw-redirect" title="Plymouth R.L.F.C">Plymouth Titans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Exeter_Centurions" title="Exeter Centurions">Exeter Centurions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Torquay" title="Torquay">Devon Sharks</a> from Torquay, North Devon Raiders from Barnstaple and <a href="/wiki/East_Devon_Eagles" title="East Devon Eagles">East Devon Eagles</a> from Exmouth. They all play in the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_Conference" title="Rugby League Conference">Rugby League Conference</a>.\n</p><p>Devon also boasts a <a href="/wiki/Field_hockey" title="Field hockey">field hockey</a> club who play in the <a href="/wiki/English_Hockey_League" class="mw-redirect" title="English Hockey League">National Premier League</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Exeter_Hockey_Club" title="University of Exeter Hockey Club">University of Exeter Hockey Club</a>\n</p><p>Horse Racing, particularly <a href="/wiki/Point_to_point_(steeplechase)" class="mw-redirect" title="Point to point (steeplechase)">point to point</a> racing and <a href="/wiki/National_Hunt" class="mw-redirect" title="National Hunt">National Hunt</a> Racing is also popular in the county, with two National Hunt racecourses (Exeter and Newton Abbot), and numerous point to point courses. There are also many successful professional racehorse trainers based in Devon.\n</p><p>The county is represented in <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a> by <a href="/wiki/Devon_County_Cricket_Club" title="Devon County Cricket Club">Devon County Cricket Club</a>, who play at a <a href="/wiki/Minor_counties_of_English_and_Welsh_cricket" title="Minor counties of English and Welsh cricket">Minor counties</a> level.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Devonians">Devonians</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Devonians">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Notable_people_from_Devon" class="mw-redirect" title="Notable people from Devon">Notable people from Devon</a></div>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Agatha_Christie.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Agatha_Christie.png/170px-Agatha_Christie.png" width="170" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cf/Agatha_Christie.png 1.5x" data-file-width="197" data-file-height="197" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Agatha_Christie.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Agatha_Christie" title="Agatha Christie">Agatha Christie</a>, best selling crime novelist</div></div></div>\n<p>Devon is known for its <a href="/wiki/Mariner" class="mw-redirect" title="Mariner">mariners</a>, such as Sir <a href="/wiki/Francis_Drake" title="Francis Drake">Francis Drake</a>, Sir <a href="/wiki/Humphrey_Gilbert" title="Humphrey Gilbert">Humphrey Gilbert</a>, Sir <a href="/wiki/Richard_Grenville_(Elizabethan_sailor)" class="mw-redirect" title="Richard Grenville (Elizabethan sailor)">Richard Grenville</a>, Sir <a href="/wiki/Walter_Raleigh" title="Walter Raleigh">Walter Raleigh</a>, and Sir <a href="/wiki/Francis_Chichester" title="Francis Chichester">Francis Chichester</a>. <a href="/wiki/Henry_Every" title="Henry Every">Henry Every</a>, described as the most notorious pirate of the late 17th century, was probably born in the village of <a href="/wiki/Newton_Ferrers" title="Newton Ferrers">Newton Ferrers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> John Oxenham (1536\xe2\x80\x931580) was a lieutenant of Drake but considered a pirate by the Spanish. <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Morton_(colonist)" title="Thomas Morton (colonist)">Thomas Morton</a> (1576\xe2\x80\x931647) was an avid Elizabethan outdoorsman probably born in Devon who became an attorney for The Council For New England, and built the New England fur-trading-plantation called Ma-Re Mount or Merrymount around a West Country-style Maypole, much to the displeasure of Pilgrim and Puritan colonists. Morton wrote a 1637 book <i>New English Canaan</i> about his experiences, partly in verse, and may have thereby become America\'s first poet to write in English.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Another famous mariner and Devonian was <a href="/wiki/Robert_Falcon_Scott" title="Robert Falcon Scott">Robert Falcon Scott</a>, the leader of the unfortunate <a href="/wiki/Terra_Nova_Expedition" title="Terra Nova Expedition">Terra Nova Expedition</a> to reach the geographical <a href="/wiki/South_Pole" title="South Pole">South Pole</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The poet <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Taylor_Coleridge" title="Samuel Taylor Coleridge">Samuel Taylor Coleridge</a>, the crime writer <a href="/wiki/Agatha_Christie" title="Agatha Christie">Agatha Christie</a>, the Irish writer <a href="/wiki/William_Trevor" title="William Trevor">William Trevor</a>, and the poet <a href="/wiki/Ted_Hughes" title="Ted Hughes">Ted Hughes</a> lived in Devon. The painter and founder of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Academy" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Academy">Royal Academy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sir_Joshua_Reynolds" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Joshua Reynolds">Sir Joshua Reynolds</a>, was born in Devon. <a href="/wiki/Chris_Dawson_(businessman)" title="Chris Dawson (businessman)">Chris Dawson</a>, the billionaire owner of retailer <a href="/wiki/The_Range_(retailer)" title="The Range (retailer)">The Range</a> was born in Devon, where his business retains its head office in <a href="/wiki/Plymouth" title="Plymouth">Plymouth</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chris_Martin_%2B_Guitar,_2011_(1,_cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Chris_Martin_%2B_Guitar%2C_2011_%281%2C_cropped%29.jpg/170px-Chris_Martin_%2B_Guitar%2C_2011_%281%2C_cropped%29.jpg" width="170" height="251" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Chris_Martin_%2B_Guitar%2C_2011_%281%2C_cropped%29.jpg/255px-Chris_Martin_%2B_Guitar%2C_2011_%281%2C_cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Chris_Martin_%2B_Guitar%2C_2011_%281%2C_cropped%29.jpg/340px-Chris_Martin_%2B_Guitar%2C_2011_%281%2C_cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1620" data-file-height="2388" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chris_Martin_%2B_Guitar,_2011_(1,_cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Chris_Martin" title="Chris Martin">Chris Martin</a>, lead singer of <a href="/wiki/Coldplay" title="Coldplay">Coldplay</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The actor <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Goode" title="Matthew Goode">Matthew Goode</a> was raised in Devon, and <a href="/wiki/Bradley_James" title="Bradley James">Bradley James</a>, also an actor, was born there. The singer <a href="/wiki/Joss_Stone" title="Joss Stone">Joss Stone</a> was brought up in Devon and frontman <a href="/wiki/Chris_Martin" title="Chris Martin">Chris Martin</a> from the British rock group <a href="/wiki/Coldplay" title="Coldplay">Coldplay</a> was born there. <a href="/wiki/Matt_Bellamy" title="Matt Bellamy">Matt Bellamy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominic_Howard" title="Dominic Howard">Dominic Howard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Wolstenholme" title="Chris Wolstenholme">Chris Wolstenholme</a> from the English group <a href="/wiki/Muse_(band)" title="Muse (band)">Muse</a> all grew up in Devon and formed the band there. Dave Hill of rock band <a href="/wiki/Slade" title="Slade">Slade</a> was born in <a href="/wiki/Flete_House" title="Flete House">Flete House</a> which is in the South Hams district of Devon. Singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Ben_Howard" title="Ben Howard">Ben Howard</a> grew up in <a href="/wiki/Totnes" title="Totnes">Totnes</a>, a small town in Devon. Another famous Devonian is the model and actress <a href="/wiki/Rosie_Huntington-Whiteley" title="Rosie Huntington-Whiteley">Rosie Huntington-Whiteley</a>, who was born in <a href="/wiki/Plymouth" title="Plymouth">Plymouth</a> and raised in <a href="/wiki/Tavistock" title="Tavistock">Tavistock</a>. The singer and songwriter <a href="/wiki/Rebecca_Newman" title="Rebecca Newman">Rebecca Newman</a> was born and raised in Exmouth.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Roger_Deakins" title="Roger Deakins">Roger Deakins</a>, called \xe2\x80\x9cthe pre-eminent <a href="/wiki/Cinematographer" title="Cinematographer">cinematographer</a> of our time", was born and lives in Devon.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Roger_Deakins_Feb-2011_02_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Roger_Deakins_Feb-2011_02_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Roger_Deakins_Feb-2011_02_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="170" height="189" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Roger_Deakins_Feb-2011_02_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Roger_Deakins_Feb-2011_02_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Roger_Deakins_Feb-2011_02_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-Roger_Deakins_Feb-2011_02_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Roger_Deakins_Feb-2011_02_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Roger_Deakins" title="Roger Deakins">Roger Deakins</a>, acclaimed cinematographer</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Trevor_Francis" title="Trevor Francis">Trevor Francis</a>, former <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Forest_F.C." title="Nottingham Forest F.C.">Nottingham Forest</a> and <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_City_F.C." title="Birmingham City F.C.">Birmingham City</a> professional footballer, and the first English footballer to cost \xc2\xa31 million, was born and brought up in Plymouth.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Swimmer <a href="/wiki/Sharron_Davies" title="Sharron Davies">Sharron Davies</a><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> and diver <a href="/wiki/Tom_Daley" title="Tom Daley">Tom Daley</a> were born in Plymouth. The Olympic runner <a href="/wiki/Jo_Pavey" title="Jo Pavey">Jo Pavey</a> was born in Honiton.  <a href="/wiki/Peter_Cook" title="Peter Cook">Peter Cook</a> the satirist, writer and comedian was born in Torquay, Devon. <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Tigers" title="Leicester Tigers">Leicester Tigers</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_and_Irish_Lions" title="British and Irish Lions">British and Irish Lions</a> Rugby player <a href="/wiki/Julian_White" title="Julian White">Julian White</a> <a href="/wiki/MBE" class="mw-redirect" title="MBE">MBE</a> was born and raised in Devon and now farms a herd of pedigree South Devon beef cattle. The dog breeder <a href="/wiki/John_%22Jack%22_Russell" class="mw-redirect" title="John &quot;Jack&quot; Russell">John "Jack" Russell</a> was also from Devon. <a href="/wiki/Jane_McGrath" title="Jane McGrath">Jane McGrath</a>, who married Australian cricketer <a href="/wiki/Glenn_McGrath" title="Glenn McGrath">Glenn McGrath</a> was born in Paignton, her long battle with and subsequent death from breast cancer inspired the formation of the <a href="/wiki/McGrath_Foundation" title="McGrath Foundation">McGrath Foundation</a>, which is one of Australia\'s leading charities.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit Sinfonia</a></li></ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Data is collected by local authority areas (Devon, Plymouth, Torbay respectively). Total population of Devon is 1,133,742 (746,399 + 256,384 + 130,959). Total population of White British persons is 1,071,015 (708,590 + 238,263 + 124,162). Percentage of White British persons is 94.467%.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.gov.uk/government/news/lord-lieutenant-for-devon-david-fursdon">"Lord-Lieutenant for Devon: David Fursdon - Press releases"</a>. <i>GOV.UK</i>. 26 March 2015<span class="reference-accessdate">.
